Make ASP.NET Web Forms Feel Native with KendoUI Mobile|.NET|<h1>Make ASP.NET Web Forms Feel Native with KendoUI Mobile</h1> <p>In 1965, a patent was filed for a synthetic grass product that would go on to be implemented in the world&rsquo;s first indoor baseball stadium. The following year, the Houston Astrodome opened and was instantly famous for its green carpet that simulated grass. The thing is that real grass is expensive to add and even more expensive to maintain, a problem astroturf solves.</p> <p>In the world of web development, native apps can be similarly expensive to build and maintain, as can re-engineering a desktop site to work on mobile. Thankfully, like <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astroturf">Astroturf</a>, we have tools that can make a website look and feel like a native app on a mobile device but also minimize the difficulty and cost of building and maintaining. KendoUI Mobile is one such tool.</p> <p>I have a number of websites out there that were designed and built in ASP.NET with the desktop browser in mind. They&rsquo;ve been running for some time, and they just don&rsquo;t look and feel right on a phone. Any way you cut it, no matter the amount of zooming, pinching, or squinting, its a painful user experience.</p> <p>In this article, I&rsquo;m going to show you a sample ASP.NET Web Forms application and how quickly we can add capabilities for native mobile rendering with KendoUI Mobile capabilities.</p> <h2>Two options &ndash; Adaptive Rendering and Alternative Rendering</h2> <p>When building and thinking about web sites on mobile, we have two general approaches we can take in developing our user interface:</p> <ol> <li>Adaptive Rendering is an approach that builds an interface that will stretch, shrink, and shift content appropriately for any sized browser.</li> <li>Alternative Rendering is an approach that provides a new user interface specific to the needs of specific browsers, or even entire classes of browsers.</li> </ol> <p>Of course, there is a third option: do nothing and expect the mobile browsers to just get better at handling desktop sized content. This might be a good option for you, as we are finding that phones are getting larger and larger screen sizes.</p> <div><a href="http://developer.telerik.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Smartphone.jpg"><img alt="" /></a> </div> <p>The <a href="http://www.nokia.com/global/products/phone/lumia1520/">Nokia Lumia 1520</a> and <a href="http://www.samsung.com/global/microsite/galaxynote/note/index.html?type=find">Samsung Galaxy Note</a> barely fit in my pants pockets, and you won&rsquo;t find me carry a man-purse for one of these giant phones. My old websites look just fine on these giant phones, but I don&rsquo;t want to rely on my customers buying a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phablet">phablet</a> just so they can access my applications.</p> <p>In our case, we will be writing an alternative rendering for a sample web site that provides a native-like experience to mobile browsers for their specific type of device.</p> <h2>Our Sample Web Site</h2> <p>For this sample, I have mocked up a search and edit screen for a hypothetical board game shop. I love board games, so I enjoy using this sample. This will demonstrate the concepts of implementing mobile capabilities over standard search and edit screens.</p> <p>The product search screen is a simple ASP.NET <code>GridView</code> with <code>ModelBinding</code> configured:</p> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]39f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]39f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="SearchDesktop" alt="SearchDesktop" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]39f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span>The source code is very simple, with a default style applied from the Visual Studio wizard:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; <code>ModelBinding</code> attributes to specify a <code>Select</code> and <code>Update</code> method that will handle those data-access methods for this form. My <code>DynamicEntity</code> is loading templates using the <a href="http://www.nuget.org/packages/DynamicDataTemplatesCS/">DynamicDataTemplatesCS NuGet package</a>. With this package, all of the input boxes and labels will be created properly in edit mode for this BoardGame object.<br /> <br /> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]45f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]45f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="EditDesktop" alt="EditDesktop" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]45f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span><br /> <br /> <h2>Transition to a new Render Mode</h2> <p>The key ASP.NET feature that will allow me to bridge from the markup intended for Desktop browsers to one intended for Mobile browsers is called FriendlyUrls. With this feature, ASP.NET will help make URLs requested of our server look more SEO-friendly. It will automatically take a URL like this:</p> <pre><code>http://www.mywebsite.com/Products/Edit.aspx?id=2&amp;Name=Chess</code></pre> <p>&hellip;and reformat it to look something a bit more friendly like this:</p> <pre><code>http://www.mywebsite.com/Products/Edit/2/Chess</code></pre> <p>That&rsquo;s a lot easier for humans to read, and with the help of the <a href="http://www.nuget.org/packages/Microsoft.AspNet.FriendlyUrls/">FriendlyUrls NuGet package</a>, easy for ASP.NET to understand.</p> <p>To assist the <code>Get</code> method on the Edit page in fetching the appropriate value from the path, we simply add a <code>FriendlyUrlSegments</code> hint to the arguments.<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">public</code> <code style="color: #000000;">Models.BoardGame myForm_GetItem([FriendlyUrlSegments(0)]</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">int</code><code style="color: #000000;">? id)</code></span></div> </div> </p> <p>Note that I use a nullable integer for this input parameter. That allows me to add an error check scenario in my method to verify that an appropriate (if any) id was submitted to this page. I can then redirect to a &ldquo;Product Not Found&rdquo; page or handle it in some other graceful manner that makes my customers happy.</p> <p>The real feature of FriendlyUrls that I want to show you is the mobile device detection and re-routing. This means that the ASP.NET router will detect that a mobile device is requesting a page and search for a <em>.mobile.aspx page with the same base-name. For that request to that device, it will serve the content of this alternate page, and </em>not<em> the content of the </em>.aspx to the requester.</p> <p>Since ASP.NET 4.0 we have had routing in all segments of ASP.NET, including web forms. With this routing feature enabled in <code>RouteConfig.cs</code> as follows, we can take advantage of adding alternate renderings for our pages:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">public</code> <code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">static</code> <code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">void</code> <code style="color: #000000;">RegisterRoutes(RouteCollection routes)</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">{</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 12px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">routes.EnableFriendlyUrls();</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">}</code></span></div> </div> </p> <p>Now we can start to add mobile-friendly renderings into our web application without modifying our existing ASPX pages. In effect, we can add this secondary rendermode risk-free&hellip; developing a mobile version of the application next to our existing pages without disturbing them.</p> <h2>Adding Mobile Rendering</h2>To add the native mobile renderings to my site, I started adding a separate <code>Site.Mobile.Master</code> file that would contain all of the framework styling and scripting necessary for KendoUI Mobile. In this case, I added links to the public CDN instances of the CSS and JavaScript files in the KendoUI Core library:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">title</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;&lt;%: Page.Title %&gt;&lt;/</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">title</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">meta</code> <code style="color: #808080;">name</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"viewport"</code> <code style="color: #808080;">content</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"width=device-width"</code> <code style="color: #000000;">/&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">link</code> <code style="color: #808080;">href</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"<a href="http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.common.core.min.css">http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.common.core.min.css</a>"</code> <code style="color: #808080;">rel</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"stylesheet"</code> <code style="color: #000000;">/&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">link</code> <code style="color: #808080;">href</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"<a href="http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.default.min.css">http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.default.min.css</a>"</code> <code style="color: #808080;">rel</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"stylesheet"</code> <code style="color: #000000;">/&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">link</code> <code style="color: #808080;">href</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"<a href="http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.mobile.all.min.css">http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/styles/kendo.mobile.all.min.css</a>"</code> <code style="color: #808080;">rel</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"stylesheet"</code> <code style="color: #000000;">/&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">script</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">script</code> <code style="color: #808080;">src</code><code style="color: #000000;">=</code><code style="color: blue;">"<a href="http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/js/kendo.ui.core.min.js">http://cdn.kendostatic.com/2014.2.716/js/kendo.ui.core.min.js</a>"</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;&lt;/</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">script</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> </div> <br /> <p>Note the <code>ViewPort</code> meta tag. This is important to force the content to the width of the device. On a phone the browser is always the full width of the device, and is not rendered in a smaller window like on a desktop.</p> <p>I also added a small block of CSS style to force the HTML and the FORM to the full size of the device and remove any margins around the content:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;style&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color: #008200;">/* stretch the form element */</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">html, body, FORM { </code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">height</code><code style="color: #000000;">: </code><code style="color: #009900;">100%</code><code style="color: #000000;">; }</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color: #008200;">/* remove margin and padding */</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">body { </code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">margin</code><code style="color: #000000;">: </code><code style="color: #009900;">0</code><code style="color: #000000;">; </code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">padding</code><code style="color: #000000;">: </code><code style="color: #009900;">0</code><code style="color: #000000;">; }</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;/style&gt;</code></span></div> </div> </p>Next, in my master page I need to wrap the content of my child pages in a KendoUI view object so that it a correct layout is applied to the content:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; font-weight: bold;">form</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> </div> <br /> <p>The standard ASP.NET form is forced to full-size, and the content of the child page is entered into the <code>asp:ContentPlaceHolder</code> called <code>mainContent</code>. Below that, I specified the layout of the page on the device and added a nav-bar to contain the title of the page was well as a footer to contain a standard view-switcher. This <code>ViewSwitcher</code> usercontrol is deployed with FriendlyUrls and allows the end-user to easily switch between mobile and desktop renderings of the page.</p> <p>The final bit on the page, the secret sauce that tells KendoUI to start rendering, is a small block of JavaScript at the very bottom of the page, outside of the form tag:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;script&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">var</code> <code style="color: #000000;">app = </code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">new</code> <code style="color: #000000;">kendo.mobile.Application (document.getElementById(</code><code style="color: blue;">"form1"</code><code style="color: #000000;">));</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;/script&gt;</code></span></div> </div> </p>That&rsquo;s it! Now the application is ready to render any content that references this site.mobile.master page in a mobile-like manner. Let&rsquo;s look at how the mobile search page is written to present this content:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;%@ Page Title="Games for Sale" Language="C#" AutoEventWireup="true" </code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">CodeBehind="Default.mobile.aspx.cs" Inherits="KendoMobile.Products.Default_mobile" </code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">EnableViewState="false" MasterPageFile="~/Site.mobile.Master" %&gt;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">asp:ListView</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;/</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">asp:Content</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> </div> <br /> <p>This looks fairly standard for a child page. Let&rsquo;s look at the few changes that I&rsquo;ve added:</p> <ul> <li><code>ViewState</code> is turned off. This is a good practice, but especially on mobile where we don&rsquo;t want to ship all of that extra nonsense over a wireless connection. In this case, we&rsquo;re not using <code>ViewState</code> at all, so let&rsquo;s just turn it off.</li> <li>I have replaced the <code>GridView</code> with a <code>ListView</code> that is showing just the names of the board games. I could add more details to my template, and I&rsquo;ll leave that experimentation to you with the source attached at the end of this article.</li> <li>The anchor for each item links to <code>Edit/Item.ID</code> This is an example of the FriendUrl that users will see when they visit my application. It&rsquo;s much easier to manage this way.</li> <li>The link to the item has a data-rel of external, telling KendoUI to load the content as an external URL and not as another div inside this page.</li> </ul> <p>Thanks to the adaptive CSS styling of KendoUI mobile, this page will detect the type of mobile device and the mobile OS requesting content and style it appropriately. Check out how some popular phones render this page:</p> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]54f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]54f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="SearchAllPhones" alt="SearchAllPhones" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]54f1ff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span> <br />The C# action behind the <code>Get</code> method is the same as the standard search page. In fact, if I was using the same controls on this page, I could use the same code-behind across both pages. Hmmm&hellip;with a little creative planning, I was able to do just that with my <code>Edit.mobile.aspx</code> page:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px !important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;%@ Page Language="C#" AutoEventWireup="true" CodeBehind="Edit.aspx.cs" </code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 6px !important;"><code style="color:
