UI for Android out of Beta, Ready for Primetime. New Controls and a Limited Time Offer|Mobile|<p>This week marks an important milestone in Telerik&rsquo;s mobile story - it is the official release of our native mobile suites -&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/android-ui">UI for Android</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/ios-ui">UI for iOS</a>.</p> <h2>What&rsquo;s included in UI for Android?</h2> <p>This is the official release of UI for Android. All controls that are included are official and ready for production. The release contains an advanced Charting framework, a Calendar, an AppFeedback control and a demo application that is full of examples.</p> <p>Before exploring the features of each control, let&rsquo;s see what else you get with UI for Android.</p> <p><strong>Telerik Chart for Android</strong>&nbsp;was introduced with the first beta of UI for Android. Since then we&rsquo;ve been working hard to incorporate all the feedback our customers sent us. Our Charting library improved significantly over the past few months in terms of features and performance and I&rsquo;m confident that it would be of great help to anyone building data visualization applications.</p> <p>Here are some of the highlights:</p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Performance improvements and UI virtualization</span></p> <p>Backed by its advanced UI virtualization mechanism Telerik Chart (re)draws only the area that is currently visible. Using UI virtualization decreases the memory footprint of your app, makes interaction smooth and enables scenarios that require displaying live streaming data.</p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">New and improved interaction behaviors</span></p> <p><span style="line-height: 1.5;">Along with the Tooltip RadChart provides a&nbsp;</span><strong style="line-height: 1.5;">Trackball</strong><span style="line-height: 1.5;">&nbsp;behavior. This behavior displays a vertical line across the plot area as well as little visual indicators wherever the trackball line crosses a data point.&nbsp;</span></p> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]fdfdff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="640" height="360" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]fdfdff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="android_release_chart_2[1]" displaymode="Original" title="android_release_chart_2[1]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></p> <p>One of the areas in which we made significant improvements was the Pan &amp; Zoom behavior. &nbsp;We quickly recognized that if you want to enable your application users to zoom in and explore dense areas you&rsquo;d need a highly performant Pan &amp; Zoom mechanism that can provide smooth experience out of the box.</p> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]09feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="864" height="279" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]09feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="android_release_chart_3[1]" displaymode="Original" title="android_release_chart_3[1]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Financial Series and Financial Indicators</span></p> <p>With this release we introduce support for stock series &ndash; both Ohlc (Open-High-Low-Close) and Candlestick. This would enable you to visualize series that operate with special data points which hold information about each the following parameters: open, high, low, close.</p> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]15feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="240" height="427" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]15feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="android_release_chart_4[1]" displaymode="Original" title="android_release_chart_4[1]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span>&nbsp;<span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]21feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="240" height="427" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]21feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="android_release_chart_5[1]" displaymode="Original" title="android_release_chart_5[1]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></p> <p>For more advanced financial scenarios, you can display financial indicators on top of the financial series. Telerik Chart supports a wide range of indicators - Moving Average, Bands, Momentum and Volatility.</p> <p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Selection</span></p> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]2dfeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="240" height="426" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]2dfeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="android_release_chart_" displaymode="Original" title="android_release_chart_6[2]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></p> <p>With support for DataPoint and Series selection you can select either part of the series or the whole series.</p> <p>Tell us what you think of the Chart on its&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/forums/android/chart">forums&nbsp;</a>and submit your feature requests on&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a href="http://feedback.telerik.com/Project/158">feedback portal</a>.</p> <h3><strong>Telerik Examples Application</strong></h3> <p>With this release we&rsquo;re introducing&nbsp;<strong>Telerik Examples</strong>&nbsp;- an Android app that will be showcasing the usage of UI for Android in various scenarios.&nbsp;Some of the scenarios currently included are:</p> <ul> <li>Using Calendar to represent different time periods in a Weekly, Monthly or Yearly fashion.</li> <li>Using Calendar to select a range of dates.</li> <li>Visualizing data using Telerik Chart&rsquo;s various series: Line, Area, Bar, Pie.</li> <li>Visualizing financial data using Telerik Chart&rsquo;s support for Financial Series and Indicators.</li> <li>Explore the details in a data set by using Telerik Chart&rsquo;s support for pinch-to-zoom and pan gestures.</li> <li>Data annotations in Telerik Chart.</li> <li>Providing feedback using Telerik&rsquo;s AppFeedback component. AppFeedback enables two-way communication between the application developer and the user.</li> </ul> <p>Telerik Examples is available for&nbsp;<a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.telerik.examples">download from Google Play</a>. The source code of the app is&nbsp;<a href="https://github.com/telerik/Android-samples/tree/master/Telerik-Examples">available on GitHub</a>.</p> <div style="text-align: center;"> <hr size="0" width="100%" align="center" /> </div> <h2>Why choose UI for Android?</h2> <p>Telerik is still new to the Android community but this does not change the fact that over the years we became experts in making developers more productive by providing the best tools on the market. With our constantly expanding portfolio we learned how to reuse our knowledge across technologies in the most efficient way. &nbsp;</p> <p>On a quick side note, we announced UI for Windows Phone in March, 2011. One year later, UI for Windows 8 became the first commercial library on the market. If you&rsquo;re interested, here&rsquo;s a&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-phone/showcases.aspx">showcase gallery</a>&nbsp;with some of the apps people are building with UI for Windows Phone.</p> <p>Finding the right tools when creating an Android app can be a hustle. Top 5 Reasons to Use Cloud Controls in your next Windows Phone 8 App|Cloud|<p>Introduction</p> <p>Back in June, we released our first ever&nbsp;<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/windowsphoneteam/posts/13-06-27/the-first-ever-cloud-powered-controls-for-windows-phone">cloud-powered controls for Windows Phone</a>. We were the first vendor to see the needs of Windows Phone developers for cloud based controls and have continued to invest in new controls and features ever since. While a majority of developers have started using this functionality, some have wondered what the benefits of using it over traditional methods are. We will begin here by examining 5 reasons to use cloud controls in your next Windows Phone 8 app.</p> <p><strong>1. Low or NO Cost of Entry</strong></p> <p>Whenever someone hears the word, &ldquo;Cloud&rdquo;, they automatically assume it is expensive and the pricing model will be very confusing. At Telerik, we want you to be successful as a developer and have laid out very clear instructions on our pricing model. With every subscription of RadControls for Windows Phone, you automatically get our &ldquo;Starter plan&rdquo;, which is completely free. This allows you up to 100MB of data storage, 5GB of bandwidth and 1 GB of file storage. To assist you further, we have unlimited API calls and all incoming bandwidth is free. If you need more storage, then check out our vast variety of plans located at the bottom of the page&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-phone/overview/all-controls/clouddataform.aspx">here</a>.</p> <p><strong>2. Maximize Developer Time Efficiency</strong></p> <p>Cloud Controls enables you (the developer) to extend your Windows Phone application with cloud functionality without having to write the control or the pieces that talk to the backend by yourself. Our cloud controls cover common cloud related scenarios like User Authentication, User Registration, Picture Upload, Picture Browsing, CRUD operations on data, In-App Notifications, etc. The Telerik Cloud Controls for Windows Phone are easily set up via a Visual Studio project template that adds the needed Telerik references as well as generates the required code to connect to our backend service. This saves you a great amount of time in getting started where you can focus on your core business logic.</p> <p><strong>3. No More Storage Wars</strong></p> <p>We&rsquo;ve all been there before. We write an app that takes advantage of Isolated Storage and everything works fine until our end-user decides to restore or upgrade their phone or uninstall our app. If they restore or upgrade their phone, then Microsoft will take care of downloading the app onto their device again. What it will not take care of is the data that we persisted in IsolatedStorage. For an app that may be used to take notes, weight measurements, etc. that data is crucial to the end-user. By using cloud controls, that data is safely stored in the cloud and can be retrieved very easily. This not only makes our end-users happy, but helps our apps to get better ratings which in turn will result in better sales.</p> <p><strong>4. Keep Your Data Safe</strong></p> <p>Mobile devices are easily lost and anyone can pick up your phone and open your app. Even if you password protect your phone with a PIN, that doesn&rsquo;t necessary mean a hacker cannot break into it and access your data. By using components such as&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-phone/overview/all-controls/cloudlogin.aspx">CloudLogin</a>, your end-user would need to login to your app to access the data.<br /> <br /> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]83feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]83feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="4_thumb-1-07C867F684F4" alt="4_thumb-1-07C867F684F4" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]83feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span> </p> <p><strong>5. Caring is Sharing</strong></p> <p>With various social media networks and more and more connected devices, we are all sharing information all the time. From breaking news stories to what we ate for dinner last night, people tend to love to share. With cloud components, you may wish to share a grocery list with your spouse, or a picture taken from your smartphone. Your company may wish to create a private portal that enables employees to share ideas on upcoming projects from their mobile device or PC/Mac. Cloud controls enable such functionality that allows us to stay connected at all times.<br /> <br /> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]8ffeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]8ffeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="5_thumb-1-10463C613585" alt="5_thumb-1-10463C613585" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]8ffeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span> </p> <p>Conclusion</p> <p>To recap the &ldquo;Top 5 Reasons to Use Cloud Controls in Your Next Windows Phone App&rdquo;:</p> <ol> <li>Low or NO Cost of Entry</li> <li>Maximize Developer Time Efficiency</li> <li>No More Storage Wars</li> <li>Keep Your Data Safe</li> <li>Caring is sharing</li> </ol> <p>Today we looked at 5 reasons to use Cloud Components in your next Windows Phone app. If you still haven&rsquo;t tried Cloud Controls for Windows Phone, you can go to your Telerik account and download the Q2 2013 SP1 release. As stated earlier, it comes complete with project templates to get you started as well as CTP versions of the controls. You may also wish to download the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.windowsphone.com/en-us/store/app/telerik-cloud-examples/cbc7a769-0b0e-4444-88c9-f869bf347457">cloud control showcase</a>application to get a better understanding of how these controls fit into your next application. If you have any questions or comments, then please leave them below.</p> <p>-Michael Crump (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/mbcrump">mbcrump</a>)</p>
Fix for Newtonsoft.Json.dll not being added to Teleriks WP Cloud Apps|Cloud|<h3>Introduction</h3> <p>On some machines, if you are using our Cloud Components, then you may get the following error as shown in&nbsp;<strong>Figure 1</strong>:</p> <p><em>System.IO.FileNotFoundException: Could not load file or assembly 'Newtonsoft.Json, Version=4.5.0.0, Culture=neutral, PublicKeyToken=30ad4fe6b2a6aeed' or one of its dependencies. The system cannot find the file specified.<br /> <br /> <span class="sfImageWrapper" data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]b7feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><a href="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]b7feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b"><img openoriginalimageonclick="true" title="error_wp_thumb-4-" alt="error_wp_thumb-4-" displaymode="Original" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]b7feff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" /></a></span><br /> <br /> <strong>Figure 1:</strong>&nbsp;Newtonsoft.Json.dll missing </em></p> <p>This indicates that the Newtonsoft.Json.dll was not added to the .XAP file.</p> <h3>The Fix</h3> <p>You can easily fix this by right-clicking on the project and selecting &ldquo;<strong>Unload Project</strong>&rdquo;, and then &ldquo;<strong>Edit YOUR_APP_NAME.csproj</strong>&rdquo;. important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 3px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">HintPath</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;$(TelerikWP8Dir)\Binaries\WindowsPhone\x86\Newtonsoft.Json.dll&lt;/</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">HintPath</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;">&nbsp;</span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">&lt;/</code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">Reference</code><code style="color: #000000;">&gt;</code></span></div> </div> </div> </div> </p> <p>Here, we will fix the ARM and the x86 version by adding &lt;Private&gt;True&lt;/Private&gt;.</p> <p>The&nbsp;<a href="http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/vstudio/bb629388.aspx">documentation</a>&nbsp;states that the Private build property: Specifies whether the reference should be copied to the output folder.</p> <p>Save the file and reload the project. You can now build and deploy the app to the emulator and you should not have that error.</p> <p> </p>
4 Extensions and Apps that Fill the Gaps in Chrome DevTools|Web|<p>Do a search online for &ldquo;must have chrome extensions/applications&rdquo; or &ldquo;top XX chrome extensions/applications&rdquo; for front-end developers and you will most certainly find several cliche articles containing a random curated list of extensions/applications. It is pretty much what you might expect to find. I am not going to write one of those articles. What follows, I hope, is more useful and insightful&nbsp;than that.</p> <p>In this article we&rsquo;ll examine twelve or so Chrome extensions/applications (mostly&nbsp;<a href="https://docs.google.com/spreadsheet/ccc?key=0AhC7l0uoKsxydENPRDRXMWhBNW9Ob3hCX08zSm41Q3c&amp;usp=drive_web#gid=0">extracted from this developer survey</a>) that will fill a few of the gaps left behind by the Devtools. Of course in order to realize the gaps left behind by the Devtools, a developer must first acquire an in depth working knowledge of the DevTools themselves. So, let&rsquo;s talk about getting good with DevTools first before we talk about extending Chrome with front-end development aids.</p> <h2>Getting Good With The Chrome DevTools</h2> <p>The Chrome developer tools provide a rich set of tools for doing web development. Hopefully, minimally, you already knew this. If not, well you&rsquo;re still reading the right article, read on.</p> <p>To gain a comprehensive working knowledge of the Devtools, one should start by reading the&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.chrome.com/devtools/index">documents provided by Google</a>. This recommendation might bestow upon me the &ldquo;Captain Obvious&rdquo; crown, but seriously, read the docs! If you have tried reading them in the past and have felt they were lacking, try again. Much has improved. By stopping now and taking the time to read the docs carefully, in depth, and with the necessary focus to fully grokk the Devtools I am certain that you will avoid installing extensions and apps that are inferior to the DevTools and duplicate functionality already provided.</p> <p>Once you have gotten your fill of the official docs, the next best place to turn for learning would be video training. Watch the free&nbsp;<a href="http://discover-devtools.codeschool.com/">&ldquo;Discover-DevTools&rdquo; course</a>&nbsp;provided by&nbsp;<a href="http://codeschool.com/">codeschool.com</a>. Or, if you are a high roller, drop da bling on the &ldquo;<a href="http://beta.pluralsight.com/courses/chrome-developer-tools">Using The Chrome Developer Tools</a>&rdquo; course by&nbsp;<a href="http://pluralsight.com/">Pluralsight</a>. It&rsquo;s good.</p> <p>If formal video training isn&rsquo;t your thing, you can always watch&nbsp;<a href="http://www.youtube.com/results?search_query=devtools">whatever filters to the top on YouTube</a>.&nbsp;<a href="http://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLS3jzvALRSe6uP9gVfXLCG6nWo7M0hAJY">Some high quality insights</a>&nbsp;from&nbsp;<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S9sktFzL3tQ">several developer conferences</a>&nbsp;can be found on YouTube regarding Devtools.</p> <p>If watching a video is mind bogglingly slow in comparison to your cheeta like reading skills? You can always piece together a selection of&nbsp;<a href="http://www.html5rocks.com/en/search?q=devtools">DevTools articles from HTML5 Rocks</a>&nbsp;to gain insight into the Devtools not found in the docs.</p> <p>Don&rsquo;t enjoy reading or watching when learning new technologies? At the very least, make sure you open up the DevTools and play with them like a 3 year old child plays with power windows. Just make sure to roll the window up and down enough to thoroughly understand everything that is provided by the DevTools.</p> <p>My parting advice for getting good with the DevTools is to open the&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.chrome.com/devtools/docs/settings">Settings UI in Devtools</a>&nbsp;and acquaint yourself with each and every setting (protip: make sure &ldquo;Disable cache while Devtools is open&rdquo; is checked).&nbsp;<a href="http://developer.telerik.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/devtools_settings.jpg"><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]abfeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="701" height="566" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]abfeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="devtools_settings[2]" displaymode="Original" title="devtools_settings[2]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></a></p> <p>Make sure you know the when&rsquo;s and the why&rsquo;s of the DevTools settings. It&rsquo;s just a fact that a keen awareness of what is provided in DevTools Settings can eliminate the false necessity found in a great deal of Chrome extensions you might otherwise be tempted to install.</p> <p>Now that you are a DevTools whiz, let&rsquo;s discuss augmenting Chrome for front-end development where the DevTools and Chrome itself come up short.</p> <h2>I&rsquo;m a Chrome DevTools Whiz But Something Is Missing.</h2> <p>With a scholarly understanding of DevTools completed (DO IT!), let&rsquo;s turn to a small list of extensions and applications that a front-end developer might install to augment the DevTools and Chrome. Gifs, FTW!).</p> <div> <p style="text-align: right;">Note: ext =&nbsp;<a href="https://chrome.google.com/webstore/category/ext/11-web-development?hl=en">Chrome Extension</a>&nbsp;and app =&nbsp;<a Instead, consider it a quick and dirty way to resize the screen in a pinch. For mobile focused development, make sure you are using the&nbsp;<a href="https://developer.chrome.com/devtools/docs/mobile-emulation">Mobile emulation</a>&nbsp;provided by the DevTools (Pro Tip: Checkout the advancements for doing&nbsp;<a href="http://www.elijahmanor.com/enhanced-chrome-emulation-tools/">emulation in DevTools Canary</a>).</p> <h3><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]dafeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]dafeff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" displaymode="Original" alt="resizer[1]" title="resizer[1]" /></span></h3> <h2>Conclusion</h2> <p>In this article, I first and foremost hope that I&rsquo;ve made it emphatically clear that you need to become a Devtools aficionado, and secondly, a connoisseur of Chrome extensions and applications.</p> <p>Before you run out and start installing the short list of extensions and applications I&rsquo;ve highlighted in this article, I&rsquo;d like to suggest switching to&nbsp;<a href="http://www.google.com/intl/en/chrome/browser/canary.html">Chrome Canary</a>&nbsp;for development if you have not already done so. Having the latest and greatest as soon as you can has it&rsquo;s benefits, but be aware&nbsp;<a href="http://www.google.com/intl/en/chrome/browser/canary.html">Canary can &ldquo;sometimes break down completely&rdquo;</a>. However, getting ahold of the latest advancements being made in regards to the Devtools, in my experience, has been worth the risk. In other words, the DevTools bleeding edge will often contain helpful solutions you need today.</p> <p>As always, If you think I&rsquo;ve missed a monumental application or extension critical to front-end development, please share them in the comments with details on why you think it&rsquo;s important. The impact of Windows 8|Desktop|<p><strong>(This article is a re-post from the&nbsp;<a title="Telerik Watch" href="http://www.telerikwatch.com/2011/06/impact-of-windows-8.html">Telerik Watch</a>&nbsp;blog by Todd Anglin)</strong></p> <p>By now, you've no doubt seen the first preview of Microsoft's follow-up to the hit Windows 7 release (if not,&nbsp;<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=p92QfWOw88I" target="_blank">take five minutes and check-out the video on YouTube</a>&nbsp;- don't worry, it's "official" and not a leak). Windows 8 finally has a name and a face, and we finally have a (public) glimpse of where Microsoft is driving the modern OS experience. The preview does not dive deep or provide the full story for Windows 8 (expect more details as Microsoft marches towards the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.buildwindows.com/" target="_blank">September Windows 8 "BUILD" conference</a>), but it does highlight some interesting facets of Microsoft's plan you should start to think about as a developer.</p> <h2>Win8 Preview Summary</h2> <p>For in-depth analysis of the the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.winsupersite.com/article/windows8/steven-sinofsky-d9-136336" target="_blank">live D9 Windows 8 preview</a>, and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.winsupersite.com/article/windows8/windows-8-preview-analysis-public-unveiling-136340" target="_blank">analysis of the follow-up preview in the aforementioned YouTube video</a>, Windows "super fan" Paul Thurott has your ticket. Microsoft RD and long-time Microsoft insider&nbsp;<a href="http://reddevnews.com/blogs/redmond-review/2011/06/wbred_windows-8.aspx" target="_blank">Andrew Brust also has some interesting commentary on RDN</a>. I'll leave the reporting to the reporters, and simply highlight some of the bigger revelations to come out of this week's news so we're all on the same page:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Windows codenamed "Windows 8" will not ship this fall</strong>&nbsp;(no surprise)</li> <li><strong>Win8 will offer a new Windows Phone 7 like "Start" experience</strong>&nbsp;(tile view)    <ul> <li>Further, according to the D9 Q&amp;A, it will not be something that can be turned-off. (We'll see about that&hellip;)</li> </ul> </li> <li><strong>Win8 will still offer "full Windows" (aka Explorer) to run "real apps"</strong> <ul> <li>Also according to D9 Q&amp;A, OEMs will not be able to prevent/hide access to "full Windows." (We'll see about that&hellip;)</li> </ul> </li> <li><strong>The new Win8 experience will feature HTML5/JavaScript "app" experiences</strong> <ul> <li>Sinofsky has not ruled-out Silverlight, though. He defended Silverlight at D9, so we'll just have to wait and see how that mixes with this story&hellip;</li> </ul> </li> <li><strong>Win8 is fully embracing Metro UI theme and touch input</strong></li> </ol> <h2>Look Past the Hype</h2> <p>Understandably, a lot of people are very excited by this week's Windows 8 preview. What's being shown is very new (for Windows), and uncharacteristically bold for Microsoft. It's amazing how many people seemed to need this preview to avoid full-out Microsoft depression.</p> <p>It's important to remember, however, that this is&nbsp;<em>not</em>&nbsp;the first of Windows 8 we've seen. Active industry watchers have been&nbsp;<a href="http://www.winsupersite.com/article/windows8/windows-8-secrets-130039" target="_blank">leaking bits-and-pieces of Windows 8</a>&nbsp;for the better part of the the last year (much to Microsoft's displeasure). From those leaks and other information shared by Microsoft in that period, we also know this about Windows 8:</p> <ol> <li>It's being built to run on Intel, AMD and (most importantly)&nbsp;<a href="http://www.zdnet.com/blog/microsoft/ces-microsoft-shows-off-windows-8-on-arm/8339" target="_blank">ARM chips</a></li> <li>It won't require any additional horsepower beyond Win7 (in some cases, less)</li> <li>It will likely integrate (to some degree) with&nbsp;<a href="http://www.pcworld.com/article/200042/windows_8_rumored_features_your_pc_your_way.html" target="_blank">WebCams/Kinect</a></li> <li>It&nbsp;<em>may</em>&nbsp;feature more integration with&nbsp;<a href="http://www.zdnet.com/blog/btl/internal-microsoft-video-shows-plans-for-next-gen-gaming-experience/46176" target="_blank">Xbox/Xbox Live/Xbox Avatars</a></li> <li>It&nbsp;<em>definitely</em>&nbsp;will feature more native integration with social media (twitter, Facebook)</li> <li>It will feature direct integration with a Windows (App) Store (confirmed this week)</li> <li>It will likely feature a renewed cloud integration story (based on Azure)</li> <li>It will focus on delivering super fast start-up, sleep, and wake times</li> <li>It will likely use the Ribbon UI throughout Windows Explorer</li> <li>It will offer native support for&nbsp;<a href="http://www.winsupersite.com/article/windows8/windows-8-secrets-news-web-135842" target="_blank">mounting ISOs</a>&nbsp;(finally!)</li> </ol> <p>Those last two items are small, but important. Mounting ISOs or using Explorer are features that only matter when you're still using "traditional" Windows. The new "Start experience" getting the attention this week is cool, sure, but Microsoft is not forgetting, abandoning, or even stalling "traditional" Windows evolution. This is still Windows at the end of the day, the OS powering millions of business machines, and that core experience will continue to incrementally improve with Win8.</p> <p>What Microsoft is showing now is a recognition that it needs to do something dramatic to re-win the hearts and minds of Windows<em>consumers</em>. It needs something to stem the flood of computing happening increasingly on non-Windows devices. It's an important piece of Window's future, but not the only piece.</p> <h2>The Gloves Are Off</h2> <p>What many observers are failing to key-in on with these Windows 8 details is that this is the first time, in a&nbsp;<em>long&nbsp;</em>time, that Microsoft is evolving Windows without the anti-trust consent decree settlement hanging over their heads. In 2002, to avoid splitting the company, Microsoft settled it's long anti-trust battle with the government, agreeing to a number of constraints that have limited Window's ability to evolve aggressively. Those limits&nbsp;<a href="http://seattletimes.nwsource.com/html/microsoft/2015029604_microsoft12.html" target="_blank">expired last month</a>, so now Microsoft, in a landscape where Windows is clearly no longer a monopoly, is freer to make some aggressive moves.</p> <p>Like what?</p> <p>Well, the limits imposed in 2002 essentially said that Microsoft could not exclude competitors from Windows, and conversely, that it must make Windows interoperate with non-Microsoft software. The net effect has been that it is difficult for Microsoft to build vertically integrated solutions because doing so could be perceived as excluding competitors.</p> <p>With that regulation now a footnote in the history books, Microsoft can theoretically pursue vertically integrated strategies that have made rivals Apple and (to a lesser degree) Google very successful over the last 10 years. For example:</p> <ul> <li>Maybe Microsoft will introduce tighter integration between Windows Phone, Windows "Slate" (or Tablet or Pad or whatever), and Windows PC.</li> <li>Microsoft&nbsp;<em>should</em>&nbsp;finally be able to add features to Windows that have been conspicuously missing (like mounting ISOs, and maybe a native PDF reader, or more robust unzipping tools).</li> <li>Microsoft might finally start shipping Windows with more of its "core experience" software pre-installed or embedded, like Live Writer (which I'm using now), Zune media experiences, or maybe even Silverlight. And let's not forget that $8.5 billion Skype purchase. We can virtually count on that playing some role in Microsoft's evolving Windows strategy.</li> </ul> <p>Whatever the case, Microsoft is finally free to boldly create experiences that are "better with Microsoft" rather than always creating vanilla solutions designed to support everyone equally.</p> <h2>Bottom Line Windows 8 Impact</h2> <p>With the hype stripped away, and the full perspective in focus, what is the bottom line impact of the Windows 8 news up to this point? What is the real value in this week's very early preview? I think there are a few important takeaways:</p> <ol> <li><strong>Windows 8 is being designed for a multi form-factor world</strong>&nbsp;There is a reason most of the demos of Windows 8 so far have been on touch-enabled, ARM-powered, "ultra mobile" devices. Microsoft is making it clear that Win8 is not a "PC" operating system with some device "layers" added last minute. Instead, Microsoft is showing that at its core, Win8 is being designed for different form-factors, processors, and input models. If nothing else, this week's preview plainly signals how Microsoft will bring Windows to tablets, and phones (maybe even replacing what we know as Windows Phone 7 today), while carrying traditional PCs in to the future.</li> <li><strong>Windows 8 is a renewed push to bring more people in to the Microsoft developer ranks&nbsp;</strong>In 2000, Microsoft introduced a brand new way to develop for Windows called .NET. At the time, Java was starting to takeover the Enterprise, and Microsoft needed a language to bring Java developers in to its camp and help reinforce its position in corporate computing. Now, roughly a decade later, Microsoft is watching consumer computing drive the success of phones and tablets, and they're eyeing the HTML5 push by powerful competitors, like Google. Making HTML5 and JavaScript a core part of the Windows 8 strategy does for Microsoft what .NET did 11 years ago. It makes the Microsoft platform appealing to developers with "non-Microsoft" skill sets, and potentially represents the next explosion in Microsoft developer community.</li> <li><strong>Windows 8 will be significant, but not life changing (and that's good)</strong>&nbsp;Yes, Windows 8 will deliver some significant new experiences, it will embrace some new developer languages, and it will extend the reach of Microsoft to the new era of computing devices. But at the end of the day, it's Windows under the hood. Your apps will still run. Silverlight will still run. WinForms will still run. The changes coming to Windows 8 help propel Windows in to the future of computing, but they don't equate to a Windows reboot. Windows 8 is about new opportunities, not about changing the way things are done.</li> </ol> <p>Don't get lost in the emotional buzz of this week's preview. Enjoy it for what it is- an early preview- but then turn to level-heads and facts to see how this all fits the bigger picture. As long-time Microsoft partners, and experts in providing solutions for Microsoft developers, you can be sure Telerik is at the front of the Windows 8 process and you can turn to us to provide our informed analysis of Microsoft's directions.</p> <p>Until then, have fun with the Windows 8 preview and start planning your travel for&nbsp;<a href="http://www.buildwindows.com/" target="_blank">Anaheim in September</a>!</p>
5 Strategies for Building Mobile Apps with Telerik|Web|<p>Traveling down the mobile development road can be&nbsp;<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/telerikmarketing/posts/14-05-21/everything-you-wanted-to-know-about-native-hybrid-and-web-apps-but-were-afraid-to-ask">challenging, given the diversity of mobile projects and the diversity of strategies available to build out mobile solutions</a>. Also, understanding all of the offerings that can help a developer execute a strategy can be challenging. In this article I am going to silo Telerik&rsquo;s mobile development offerings into logical and comprehensible strategies, so that a developer can easily travel Telerik&rsquo;s mobile development road and stop off where a project&rsquo;s requirements are met.</p> <div> <p style="text-align: right;">Disclaimer: Most of these strategies assume that you want to use web technologies to build an application UI to reach as many users as possible either using the web platform (i.e. browser) or outputting several hybrid native applications (i.e. WebView) for multiple mobile platforms from a single code base of HTML, CSS, and JavaScript.</p> </div> <h2>Strategy 1: Use Kendo UI Web Widgets With Adaptive Mobile Rendering Options &amp; Kendo UI Data Visualization Widgets</h2> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]2dffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]2dffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" displaymode="Original" alt="Screenshot-2014-08-21-16.04.47-152x300[2]" title="Screenshot-2014-08-21-16.04.47-152x300[2]" style="float: right;" /></span>Both the&nbsp;<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/grid/adaptive">Grid</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/scheduler/adaptive">Scheduler</a>&nbsp;professional widgets offer a mobile setting that when set to true will adjust the widgets&rsquo; behavior and UI to adapt to phones and tablets (aka Adaptive Rendering). In addition to these two widgets containing specific phone/tablet rendering options the Web and Data Visualization widgets are supported on touch devices. This makes it possible to build a mobile/desktop web UI with the Kendo UI Web and Data Visualization widgets without actually using a Kendo UI Mobile widget.</p> <p>To get started with Kendo UI Web and Data visualization widgets, check out the&nbsp;<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/">demos</a>&nbsp;or read the&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/kendo-ui/">Getting Started</a>&nbsp;documents.</p> <h4><strong>Notes:</strong></h4> <ul> <li>The<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/grid/adaptive">Grid</a>,<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/scheduler/adaptive">Scheduler</a>, and Data Visualization widgets are part of the Professional Kendo UI Widgets sold commercially. A fully functional<a href="http://www.telerik.com/download/kendo-ui">30 day trial of Kendo UI Professional is available</a>.</li> <li>Web and Data Visualization Widgets are supported on Firefox ESR, IE 7+, Safari 5+, Chrome Latest, Opera 15+, iOS 6.0+, Android 2.3+ (In Android 2.3 dataviz widgets support only Canvas rendering mode), BlackBerry OS 10+, Windows Phone 8+, and Chrome for Android.</li> <li>This strategy is typically used to build web applications that run in a browser on a phone, tablet, or desktop (i.e. Responsive Design/Mobile First Design).</li> </ul> <h2>Strategy 2: Use Kendo UI Mobile, Web and DataViz Widgets Running On Browsers</h2> <p>Mobile widgets are not for mobile and tablet devices alone;&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/kendo-ui/getting-started/mobile/regular-usage">they can be used alongside the web and data visualization class of widgets</a>&nbsp;on a handful of browsers. Given that the mobile widgets work on several desktop browsers and many of the Web and Data Visualization widgets work on common tablet and phone browsers, a developer could construct a mobile web application using web, data visualization, and mobile widgets together, intending them to run on a web browser on mobile devices first and secondarily on desktop browsers.</p> <p>To get started with Kendo UI Mobile Widgets check out the&nbsp;<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/kendo-ui/">demos</a>&nbsp;or read the&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/kendo-ui/">Getting Started</a>&nbsp;guides.</p> <h2>Strategy 3: Use Kendo UI Mobile Application Toolkit And Mobile Widgets Running on Mobile Browsers or in WebViews</h2> <p><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]38ffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="295" height="300" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]38ffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="Screenshot-2014-08-21-16.22.23-295x300[1]" displaymode="Original" title="Screenshot-2014-08-21-16.22.23-295x300[1]" style="float: left; margin: 10px; border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span>Kendo UI offers a toolkit for building web-based mobile applications which make use of mobile widgets inside of a framework designed to run on mobile browsers. Think of the Kendo UI Mobile Application Toolkit as a mini-SPA (single page application) framework for mobile browsers. It&rsquo;s similar in design to something like&nbsp;<a href="http://jquerymobile.com/">jQuery Mobile</a>&nbsp;but much more sophisticated when it comes to building applications instead of websites.</p> <p>When the Mobile widgets are used in conjunction with the Mobile Application toolkit, it&rsquo;s assumed that the application is running on a phone or tablet device within a browser or a WebView.</p> <p>To get started with the Kendo UI Mobile Application Toolkit read the, &ldquo;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/kendo-ui/tutorials/build-apps-with-kendo-ui-mobile">Intro to Building Apps With Kendo UI Mobile</a>&rdquo; tutorial and review the API documents for&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/kendo-ui/api/mobile/application"><code>kendo.mobile.Application</code></a>.</p> <h2>Strategy 4: Use AppBuilder (Mobile Build/Development Tool) To Aid In Hybrid Native Development, Bridging Native API&rsquo;s, and Output Cross-Platform Apps</h2> <p>Using Kendo UI Mobile widgets and the Mobile Application Toolkit, a developer can build a&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/whitepapers/kendo-ui/mobile-developer-guidance-hybrid-vs.-native">native hybrid application</a>&nbsp;that is intended to simply run in a WebView. However, the developer is burdened with taking the Kendo UI mobile application and creating a native application with a WebView for each platform they would like the application to run on. Additionally, what if the application required access to a native API, like the camera? How will the developer bridge the gap between the web application in the WebView and the native environment? What&rsquo;s needed is a tool that will take in HTML, CSS, and JavaScript and output the desired (i.e. iOS, Android, Windows Phone 8) native applications and also provide access to a devices native API&rsquo;s (e.g. the devices camera).</p> <p>This is exactly where&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/platform/appbuilder/introduction/appbuilder-mobile-app-development">AppBuilder steps in solves a number of complexities associated with hybrid development</a>. In fact, solving the distribution and native API jungle is just the tip of the iceberg for AppBuilder. Appbuilder reduces the complexities associated with hybrid development and deployment.</p> <p><a href="http://developer.telerik.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/video7.gif"><br /> </a></p> <p>The best place to get started with AppBuilder is to&nbsp;<a href="https://www.telerik.com/login/v2/platform?ReturnUrl=https%3a%2f%2fidentity.telerik.com%2fv2%2foauth%2ftelerik%2fauthorize%3fclient_id%3duri%253aappshell%26redirect_uri%3dhttps%253a%252f%252fplatform.telerik.com%252f%26response_type%3dcode%26state%3dCC2B5DEBDBA87624481483AB6871ECAC9C5355C7EEBC73E08B5185F7ACEA5A8C">sign up for a free trial</a>&nbsp;and play around with the &ldquo;Friends App&rdquo; example application already set up and ready to roll. Of course,&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/platform/appbuilder/introduction/index">reading the docs</a>&nbsp;is a great place to start too.</p> <h4><span style="font-weight: normal; line-height: 1.2; font-size: 18px;">Strategy 5: Use Native Widgets to Augment Native Mobile Development done in Objective-C, Java, or C# with Native Android, iOS, Windows Widgets</span></h4> <p>A&nbsp;<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/telerikmarketing/posts/14-05-21/everything-you-wanted-to-know-about-native-hybrid-and-web-apps-but-were-afraid-to-ask">hybrid native mobile application is not always the ideal solution for a project</a>. In those situations Telerik offers Native Android, iOS, Windows Widgets to be used by Objective-C, Java, or C# developers when doing native application development.</p> <p>To get started with any of the native mobile widgets checkout one of their product pages:</p> <ul> <li><a href="http://www.telerik.com/ios-ui">iOS</a></li> <li><a href="http://www.telerik.com/android-ui">Android</a></li> <li><a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-8/overview.aspx">Windows 8 Mobile</a></li> </ul> <h2>Future Strategy: Use JavaScript via NativeScript To Build Truly Native iOS and Android applications</h2> <p>In the future, Telerik will be offering&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/nativescript">NativeScript</a>&nbsp;which intends to move closer to the ideal of building mobile applications in one language (i.e. JavaScript) that can directly use the native APIs on multiple platforms without relying on Cordova.</p> <p>NativeScript is currently available as a private preview. You can&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/nativescript-insiders-signup">sign up for the NativeScript Insiders program here</a>.</p> <h2>Conclusion</h2> <p>This article was not intended to give you in-depth working knowledge of each strategy, but more of a high level overview of Telerik solutions to help you formulate the best solution for your mobile project. It&rsquo;s my hope, minimally, that I&rsquo;ve set up a mental context for logically understanding the stops along Telerik&rsquo;s mobile development road.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p>
Make ASP.NET Web Forms Feel Native with KendoUI Mobile|Web|<p>In 1965, a patent was filed for a synthetic grass product that would go on to be implemented in the world&rsquo;s first indoor baseball stadium. The following year, the Houston Astrodome opened and was instantly famous for its green carpet that simulated grass. The thing is that real grass is expensive to add and even more expensive to maintain, a problem astroturf solves.</p> <p>In the world of web development, native apps can be similarly expensive to build and maintain, as can re-engineering a desktop site to work on mobile. Thankfully, like&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astroturf">Astroturf</a>, we have tools that can make a website look and feel like a native app on a mobile device but also minimize the difficulty and cost of building and maintaining. KendoUI Mobile is one such tool.</p> <p>I have a number of websites out there that were designed and built in ASP.NET with the desktop browser in mind. They&rsquo;ve been running for some time, and they just don&rsquo;t look and feel right on a phone. Any way you cut it, no matter the amount of zooming, pinching, or squinting, its a painful user experience.</p> <p>In this article, I&rsquo;m going to show you a sample ASP.NET Web Forms application and how quickly we can add capabilities for native mobile rendering with KendoUI Mobile capabilities.</p> <h2>Two options &ndash; Adaptive Rendering and Alternative Rendering</h2> <p>When building and thinking about web sites on mobile, we have two general approaches we can take in developing our user interface:</p> <ol> <li>Adaptive Rendering is an approach that builds an interface that will stretch, shrink, and shift content appropriately for any sized browser.</li> <li>Alternative Rendering is an approach that provides a new user interface specific to the needs of specific browsers, or even entire classes of browsers.</li> </ol> <p>Of course, there is a third option: do nothing and expect the mobile browsers to just get better at handling desktop sized content. This might be a good option for you, as we are finding that phones are getting larger and larger screen sizes:</p> <p style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://developer.telerik.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/08/Smartphone.jpg"><span data-sfref="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]72ffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" class="sfImageWrapper"><img width="700" height="404" src="[images|OpenAccessDataProvider]72ffff31-ebfb-67f3-ba7d-ff000072e94b" alt="Smartphone[2]" displaymode="Original" title="Smartphone[2]" style="border-width: 0px; border-style: solid;" /></span></a></p> <p style="text-align: center;">Huge phones</p> <p>The&nbsp;<a href="http://www.nokia.com/global/products/phone/lumia1520/">Nokia Lumia 1520</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.samsung.com/global/microsite/galaxynote/note/index.html?type=find">Samsung Galaxy Note</a>&nbsp;barely fit in my pants pockets, and you won&rsquo;t find me carry a man-purse for one of these giant phones. My old websites look just fine on these giant phones, but I don&rsquo;t want to rely on my customers buying a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phablet">phablet</a>&nbsp;just so they can access my applications.</p> <p>In our case, we will be writing an alternative rendering for a sample web site that provides a native-like experience to mobile browsers for their specific type of device.</p> <h2>Transition to a new Render Mode</h2> <p>The key ASP.NET feature that will allow me to bridge from the markup intended for Desktop browsers to one intended for Mobile browsers is called FriendlyUrls. With this feature, ASP.NET will help make URLs requested of our server look more SEO-friendly. It will automatically take a URL like this:</p> <pre><code>http://www.mywebsite.com/Products/Edit.aspx?id=2&amp;Name=Chess</code></pre> <p>&hellip;and reformat it to look something a bit more friendly like this:</p> <pre><code>http://www.mywebsite.com/Products/Edit/2/Chess</code></pre> <p>That&rsquo;s a lot easier for humans to read, and with the help of the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.nuget.org/packages/Microsoft.AspNet.FriendlyUrls/">FriendlyUrls NuGet package</a>, easy for ASP.NET to understand.</p> <p>To assist the&nbsp;<code>Get</code>&nbsp;method on the Edit page in fetching the appropriate value from the path, we simply add a<code>FriendlyUrlSegments</code>&nbsp;hint to the arguments.</p> <pre>public<code> Models</code>.<code>BoardGame </code>myForm_GetItem([FriendlyUrlSegments(0)]int?<code> id</code>)</pre> <p>Note that I use a nullable integer for this input parameter. That allows me to add an error check scenario in my method to verify that an appropriate (if any) id was submitted to this page. I can then redirect to a &ldquo;Product Not Found&rdquo; page or handle it in some other graceful manner that makes my customers happy.</p> <p>The real feature of FriendlyUrls that I want to show you is the mobile device detection and re-routing. This means that the ASP.NET router will detect that a mobile device is requesting a page and search for a&nbsp;<em>.mobile.aspx page with the same base-name. For that request to that device, it will serve the content of this alternate page, and</em><em>&nbsp;</em>not<em>&nbsp;</em><em>the content of the</em><em>&nbsp;</em>.aspx to the requester.</p> <p>Since ASP.NET 4.0 we have had routing in all segments of ASP.NET, including web forms. With this routing feature enabled in&nbsp;<code>RouteConfig.cs</code>&nbsp;as follows, we can take advantage of adding alternate renderings for our pages:</p> <pre>public<code> </code>static<code> </code>void<code> </code>RegisterRoutes(<code>RouteCollection routes</code>)<code></code></pre> <pre>{<code></code></pre> <pre><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; routes</code>.EnableFriendlyUrls();<code></code></pre> <pre>}</pre> <p>Now we can start to add mobile-friendly renderings into our web application without modifying our existing ASPX pages. In effect, we can add this secondary rendermode risk-free&hellip; developing a mobile version of the application next to our existing pages without disturbing them.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <h2>Summary</h2> <p>It&rsquo;s easy to modify an existing ASP.NET project to start adding mobile capabilities to it. If you want your application to act native, to feel native to the mobile users browsing it, give KendoUI Mobile a shot. It&rsquo;s available as part of KendoUI Core&rsquo;s Open Source package and you can add references to the Telerik CDN to start using it now. Learn more about how I wrote this and&nbsp;<a href="https://github.com/csharpfritz/KendoMobile">download the source code</a>&nbsp;for this article now:&nbsp;<a href="https://github.com/csharpfritz/KendoMobile">https://github.com/csharpfritz/KendoMobile</a>.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p>

So far, we have examined the following controls: RadCloudLogin with SocialSharing via Facebook, RadCloudRegistration and the RadCloudCalendar control. Today, we will extend the Appointment.xaml page by adding a list of appointments for the current day using RadDataBoundListBox. We will also take a look at what is involved in retrieving data from Everlive as well as adding logout functionality to the app.</p> <h4>Creating a Value Converter</h4> <p>We&rsquo;ll begin by creating a new Folder in our project called, &ldquo;<strong>Helper</strong>&rdquo;. important;"><code style="color: #000000;">}</code></span></span></div> </div> <br /> <p>Taking it from the top, we create an instance of EverliveAppointmentSource as we will be needing access to this class in other methods. We have left our Loaded event handler, except now it simply calls the DisplayAppointments method. This method will fetch new appointments with the start and end date that we specified. Since we only want the current date, we were able to simply use the DateTime class. After we have our appointments, we set the ItemSource to our RadDataBoundListBox by calling the GetAppointments method which create a collection of IAppointment objects. We can then examine that data and only display the appointments for the current date.</p> <p>Finally, the OnNavigatedTo event will initialize the CloudAppointmentSource to be used.</p> <p>If we launch the application and add several appointments to the same day, then we will see what is shown in&nbsp;<strong>Figure 2</strong>.</p> <p><strong>Figure 2:</strong>&nbsp;The Appointment.xaml page showing our appointments for the day.</p> <h4>What&rsquo;s next?</h4> <p>We&rsquo;ve extended our app by adding a list of appointments for the current day using RadDataBoundListBox. We also took a look at what is involved in retrieving data from Everlive as well as adding logout functionality to the app. But we aren&rsquo;t done yet. We are going to use the built-in design templates and add in an &ldquo;About&rdquo; page, use another Cloud component as well as add in our new Dev Center Template.</p> <p>Thanks,</p> <p>Michael Crump&nbsp;<br /> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/mbcrump">@mbcrump</a></p> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />
Resources to the Build Apps for Any Device with .NET Session|Desktop|<h3>Introduction</h3> <p>Hello everyone,</p> <p>We wanted to thank you for attending the DevCraft Q1 2014 online conference. In our first session, &ldquo;Build Apps for Any Device with .NET&rdquo; we covered how the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/devcraft">Telerik DevCraft Collection</a>&nbsp;helps you build applications for any screen. From mobile to web to desktop, we have you covered. Regardless if you are starting a new project or wanting to upgrade an existing one, our control suite will allow your users to have a great experience on any device they choose.</p> <p>We began the session by talking about mobile and how our native controls for&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-8/overview.aspx">Windows 8/8.1</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-phone.aspx">Windows Phone 8</a>&nbsp;contain a variety of controls that will help jump start your application. We then took a look at our web controls and discovered the completeness of&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/aspnet-ajax.aspx">UI for ASP.NET AJAX</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/kendo-ui">Kendo UI for MVC</a>. We wrapped up with several desktop demos covering our new&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/support/whats-new/wpf">Document processing controls</a>found in&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/wpf/overview.aspx">UI for WPF</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/support/whats-new/winforms">RadDataEntry and Analytics integration</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/winforms.aspx">UI for Windows Forms</a>.</p> <p>As promised, we&rsquo;ve included a list of questions and answers from the session below. A wrap up of the Q3 2013 AJAX webinar|Cloud|<h1>Audio, Video and the Cloud!</h1> <h1>A wrap up of the Q3 2013 AJAX webinar</h1> <p>On Monday, October 28<sup>th</sup>, I presented a webinar demonstrating the cool new controls, and some of the great features that are now available in the 2013 Q3 release of the Telerik AJAX controls.&nbsp; Many thanks to all who attended; it is always a pleasure to speak to the Telerik community about our products.</p> <p>We showed you the three new controls in this release: MediaPlayer, Lightbox, and CloudUpload.&nbsp; There were great features demonstrated for our long time favorites: the grid, editor, and scheduler.&nbsp; The new HTML chart sparklines and data navigator functionality were shown as well. Finally, I wrapped up by showing you lightweight rendering and our new &ldquo;auto mode&rdquo; for rendering the Telerik AJAX controls.</p> <p>You can review the&nbsp;<a href="http://tv.telerik.com/watch/telerik-q3-2013-webinar-week/new-in-q3-for-aspnet-ajax-audio-video-and-cloud-capabilities" title="Video recording of the AJAX Webinar" target="_blank">video recording of the webinar</a>&nbsp;at any time on Telerik TV.&nbsp; You will become one of my &ldquo;future people&rdquo;&hellip; and once you watch the webinar you will know why.&nbsp; Additionally, I have made the&nbsp;<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/docs/default-source/fritzlibrary/ajaxq3webinar.zip?sfvrsn=2" title="The source code to the samples shown in this webinar" target="_blank">source code for the samples</a>&nbsp;that I demonstrated from Visual Studio available for you to download.</p> <p>Many of you had questions during the webinar.&nbsp; Let&rsquo;s review some of the common and interesting ones:</p> <h2>New Control Questions</h2> <p>Common to All New Controls</p> <p><img width="100" src="http://blogs.telerik.com/images/default-source/asp-net-ajax/new-controls!.png?sfvrsn=2" alt="NEW CONTROLS!" title="NEW CONTROLS!" /><strong>Q: What are these new controls using to render, jquery? Will it auto register or detect if it's loaded so it doesn't double load or cause conflicts?</strong><br />A: The controls can be used with jQuery, but we primarily use standard JavaScript functions to render the controls. You can disable the built in jQuery if you'd like, as it is not required to render controls.</p> <p><strong>Q: All the new controls, which you are demoing today, can be used with VS2010 or they are compatible only with VS2013?</strong><br />A: Yes, you can use them with VS2008, VS2010, VS2012 and VS2013</p> <p><strong>Q: I entered the meeting a bit late. Just wanted to know if all the changes discussed are also targeting the 4.0 framework</strong><br />A: Yes, of course!</p> <h3><a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/aspnet-ajax/cloud-upload.aspx">Cloud Upload</a></h3> <p><strong>Q: Can Rad Cloud Upload work in a mobile app?</strong><br />A: If the app is wrapped HTML app, yes it will work. If the app is native app, you can use the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/windows-phone/overview/all-controls/cloudpictureupload.aspx">Windows Phone 8 upload control</a>. &nbsp;You can test our demos in your mobile device by navigating to&nbsp;<a href="http://demos.telerik.com/aspnet-ajax/cloud-upload/examples/overview/defaultcs.aspx">http://demos.telerik.com/aspnet-ajax/cloud-upload/examples/overview/defaultcs.aspx</a></p> <p><img width="240" src="http://blogs.telerik.com/images/default-source/asp-net-ajax/cloud-upload-services.png?sfvrsn=4" alt="Cloud Upload to Azure, S3, or Everlive" title="Cloud Upload Services" /><strong>Q: Will you support upload to Skydrive, Google Drive, SalesForce or Dropbox?</strong><br />A: We are planning to implement custom providers for the CloudUpload control. In case that there is a demand for this, we could consider to implement it out of the box.</p> <p><strong>Q: Pure client side upload is extremely valuable we are developing an ftp client applet just for this&nbsp;</strong><br />A: Thanks for the feedback. We will consider making client-side upload.<br /> <br /> <strong>Q: Any chance of adding file encryption to upload controls (outside of SSL)&nbsp;</strong><br />A: We could provide an access point in the upload handler where the developer could encrypt the uploading data.</p> <p><strong>Q: Does the Cloud upload load directly from the client to the provider or does it go through the server ?&nbsp;</strong><br />A: Hello, RadCloudUpload uploads the files to the server and then the server sends them to the Cloud. So yes, it goes through the server. We are considering the possibility of adding a client-side upload in the near future if there is enough demand.<br /> <br /> </p> <h3><a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/aspnet-ajax/media-video-player.aspx">Media Player</a></h3> <p><strong>Q: Can we use media player with a playlist?</strong><br />A: The PlayList feature is in the works right now! We will have this option for the Q1 release.</p> <p><img width="240" src="http://blogs.telerik.com/images/default-source/asp-net-ajax/media-player-sample.png?sfvrsn=2" alt="A sample media player with title and play controls" title="Media Player sample" />Q: Why would you want to use the Telerik MediaPlayer and not the YouTube video player on a web site?<br />A: This is just an option, which will allow you to easily configure RadMediaPlayer directly in Visual Studio. The main purpose of RadMediaPlayer is to provide support for file types supported by the HTML5 video and audio tags.&nbsp; Additionally, you can host your own media and present that content if your organization does not allow access to YouTube.</p> <p><strong>Q: Can the media player control display live event?</strong><br />A: In theory, this should be supported by the &lt;video&gt; tag on which the controls is based, but we need to test this. Could you please open a support ticket with this request.</p> <p><strong>Q: Is Media Player frame accurate?</strong><br />A: The player is based on the popular HTML5 &lt;video&gt; tag and the frame rate depends on the browser and the client's hardware configuration. The MediaPlayer itself does not have control over the rendering of the video steam.</p> <p><strong>Q: Will Media Player display subtitles?&nbsp;</strong><br />A: This feature is currently under consideration for implementation in one of the upcoming releases.</p> <h3><a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/aspnet-ajax/lightbox.aspx">Lightbox</a></h3> <p><strong>Q: Having markup for every img doesn&rsquo;t make sense. Th</a>e same is valid for the KendoUI MVC wrappers.&nbsp;</p> <h2>New Features for Existing Controls</h2> <h3><a href="http://www.telerik.com/products/aspnet-ajax/editor.aspx">Editor</a></h3> <p><strong>Q: Is there a means to strip specific HTML tags from the RADEditor Content?</strong><br />A: Yes, you can write a custom content filter that will strip the desired tags with a regular expression&nbsp;<a href="http:">http://demos.telerik.com/aspnet-ajax/editor/examples/contentfilters/defaultcs.aspx</a></p> <p><strong>Q: RadEditor cloud upload?</strong><br />A: We should consider firstly adding support for the CloudUpload in RadFileExplorer. Chrome, for example, can handle several thousands. The clientTemplate property is a string (that can contain HTML) that is evaluated with the data from the service</p> <h3>Common Features</h3> <p><strong>Q: Is it possible to make push requests to the client? via SignalR</strong><br />A: The control in the browser initiates a request to the corresponding service (or page method). You can use its client-side events to cancel the request and write your own. When the template is about to be databound you get another event that you can use to modify it with your own logic</p> <p><strong>Q: Why wouldn't I want to use Lightweight rendering everywhere?</strong><br />A: You may lose rounded corners and/or gradients in older browsers that do not support CSS3. Read this post for more details:<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/aspnet-ajax/posts/13-06-13/attack-of-the-light-rendered-css3-and-html5-win">http://blogs.telerik.com/aspnet-ajax/posts/13-06-13/attack-of-the-light-rendered-css3-and-html5-win</a>&nbsp;Generally, you should not have issues even with older browsers. &nbsp;<br />There is no reason not to use the Lightweight rendering everywhere. Our suggestion is to set the render mode in web.config AppSettings to Telerik.Web.UI.RenderMode = Auto. This way legacy browser will receive the old rendering and the modern browsers will receive the new rendering.</p> <p><strong>Q: What controls are supported in lightweight rendering mode?</strong><br />A: Calendar, ComboBox, Dock, FormDecorator, Menu, ToolTip, and Window.&nbsp; We&rsquo;re committed to expanding this feature in the future.&nbsp;</p> <p><strong>Q: Do all of these rich controls work well in Safari on the Macintosh?</strong><br />A: The controls should work well on Safari on MAC as well as on the mobile/touch devices with Win8 Mobile and iOS. If you experience any problems, please report them via&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/feedback/ajax">our Feedback portal</a>.</p> <p><strong>Q: Does this version of Controls support the Release version of Visual Studio 2013 RTM</strong><br />A: Yes, our controls in all of DevCraft Q3 2013 are Visual Studio 2013 ready.</p> <p><strong>Q: When will the Gantt Chart plan to be released? 2014 Q1? We have been waiting for a while. Thanks.</strong><br />A: We will do our best to deliver it as soon as possible, but it will probably be Q2 or Q3 2014.&nbsp;</p> <h2>&hellip; and of course the highlight question of the webinar</h2> <p><strong>Q: Where did you get the great Pirate hat?</strong><br />A: That is a Captain Jeff Sparrow ORIGINAL!&nbsp; Actually, I picked it up while visiting the Disney parks in Orlando, just outside of the Pirates of the Caribbean ride.</p> <h2>Summary</h2> <p>Thank you to everyone who participated in the webinar, and thank you for your interest in the Telerik ASP.NET Controls. &nbsp;You can&nbsp;<a href="http://tv.telerik.com/watch/telerik-q3-2013-webinar-week/new-in-q3-for-aspnet-ajax-audio-video-and-cloud-capabilities">watch the webinar on Telerik TV</a>&nbsp;and you can&nbsp;<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/docs/default-source/fritzlibrary/ajaxq3webinar.zip?sfvrsn=2">download the sample code</a>&nbsp;for this webinar as well so that you can follow along at home. &nbsp;Download a copy of the controls and get started with the Media Player, Lightbox, and Cloud Upload today.</p>
Using Telerik Backend Services with a WPF application-stage 1|Desktop|<h3>Intro</h3> <p>I am a football (or if you&rsquo;re American, soccer) fan. Recently, I got access to some data for the current season of the Premier League (2013/14), including things like fixtures (date, result, goals, shots, cards etc) and players (minutes played, goals, assists, cards and more). I decided to take advantage of this in order to create an application to analyze the stats to look for cool facts (like some of the things that commentators say on the TV).</p> <p>Initially, I wanted to create a WPF application that I could share with other people, with the data stored centrally. However, the data should be stored in a format that would allow me to easily access it from a mobile app in the future.</p> <p>This is where Telerik Platform comes in handy. I can store the stats in the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/backend-services">Telerik Backend</a>&nbsp;and they&rsquo;ll be easily accessible via the .Net SDK from anywhere in the planet (as long there is Internet access). And when I am ready to create my mobile app, I can use AppBuilder to create it while utilizing the same data.</p> <p>In this article, I&rsquo;ll walk through getting started building this application by looking at how to set up the Telerik Backend Services, establish my data types, import my existing data and, finally, how to get that data back out within my WPF application.</p> <h3>Data</h3> <p>Before we start working with the Telerik Backend Services, let&rsquo;s review the data that we&rsquo;ll be working with. It contains two different types: players and teams.</p> <h4>Team</h4> <p>A team contains some basic information like the team name, city and stadium name, plus fixtures that provide in depth stats of each game played so far in the season. Here is a team in JSON format.</p> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">{ </code><code style="color: blue;">"Team"</code> <code style="color: #000000;">: {</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 18px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">} ],</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 12px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">} }</code></span></span></div> </div> <br /> <h3>Getting Set up the Telerik Platform</h3> <p>The first thing we need to get started is to create a Backend Services Project on the&nbsp;<a href="https://platform.telerik.com/">Telerik Platform</a>. You can create a Backend Services Project following the&nbsp;<a href="http://docs.telerik.com/platform/help/projects/create/backend-services-project">steps from here</a>.</p> <p>Once the backend project is created we need to add new types. In order to do that, open the backend project, go to types and press &ldquo;Create a Content Type.&rdquo;</p> <h4>Creating data types in the backend</h4> <p>By default every type contains the following fields:&nbsp;<code>Id</code>,&nbsp;<code>CreatedAt</code>,&nbsp;<code>ModifiedAt</code>,&nbsp;<code>CreatedBy</code>,&nbsp;<code>ModifiedBy</code>&nbsp;and<code>Owner</code>; these fields cannot be changed or removed.</p> <p>Let&rsquo;s start by mapping the fields for our two data types. For the Team type let&rsquo;s create:</p> <ul> <li>LongName, Name, Stadium and City are of type&nbsp;<strong>Text</strong>.</li> <li>TeamId is of type&nbsp;<strong>Number</strong>.</li> <li>Fixtures of type&nbsp;<strong>Object.</strong></li> </ul> <p>When thinking about it, the&nbsp;<code>Fixtures</code>&nbsp;field probably seemed tricky, as it is a collection of complex type items containing strings, numbers and dates. However, the&nbsp;<strong>Object</strong>&nbsp;type can handle complex types very well.</p> <p>The screenshots below show the mapping for the Team and Player data types. If you are following along, feel free to copy the types for Player from those listed in the image.</p>Once that is done we are ready to set up our Visual Studio project.&nbsp;<br /> <h3>Preparing the Visual Studio project</h3> <p>The first step is to download Telerik Backend Services SDK. The SDK can be found at:<a href="https://platform.telerik.com/#downloads/backendservices">https://platform.telerik.com/#downloads/backendservices</a>. The download contains&nbsp;<code>Newtonsoft.Json</code>&nbsp;and the<code>Telerik.Everlive.Sdk</code>&nbsp;libraries and their configuration files.</p> <h4>Creating equivalent types in C#</h4> <p>In order to use the data types previously defined in the backend we need to create a class for each type. The task is rather straightforward &ndash; just follow these steps and you should be fine:</p> <ul> <li>Create a new class and give it the same name as the type in the backend service</li> <li>Include: Telerik.Everlive.Sdk.Core.Model.Base</li> <li>Make it inherit from DataItem</li> <li>For every field create a public property with a public getter and a public setter</li> <li>Make sure to create a default parameter less constructor, or have no constructor at all</li> <li>For object type fields provide a class or a collection of a matching class</li> </ul>For example, here is what my completed&nbsp;<code>Player</code>&nbsp;class looks:<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">using</code> <code style="color: #000000;">System;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">using</code> <code style="color: #000000;">System.Collections.Generic;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">using</code> <code style="color: #000000;">Telerik.Everlive.Sdk.Core.Model.Base;</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 3px ! important;">&nbsp;</span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">public</code> <code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">class</code> <code style="color: #000000;">Player : DataItem</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! This means that if your data is in the form of JSON, then your classes can be ready in a matter of moments.</p> <p><a href="http://jsonclassgenerator.codeplex.com/">http://json2csharp.com/<br />http://jsonclassgenerator.codeplex.com/</a></p> <h3>The Backend service in action</h3> <p>Before we can perform any operations on the data, we will need to get the API Key from our backend services project.</p> <p>Open the project and go to the API Keys section. Your API Key will be waiting for you in there. Copy the code as we&rsquo;ll need to place it within our code.</p> <p>Please bear in mind that you should never publish your API keys as this would allow unauthorized access to your data.</p> <h4>Sending the data into Backend</h4> <p>Writing data to the data service takes just a few steps:</p> <ul> <li>Create the data objects</li> <li>Prepare a backend service project link</li> <li>Create a facade for working with the required data store</li> <li>Export the data</li> </ul>Below is the code to export a player object to the backend service. As you can see, while I had a good game for &ldquo;Team Telerik,&rdquo; the Grumpy Squirrels got trashed 3:0! :)<br /> <br /> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">playerFacade.Create(player).ExecuteSync();</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">}</code></span></div> </div> <br />One you run this, you can view the new record in the Telerik Platform:<br /> <br /> <p>As you can see by this example, it takes more time to create a player object than to actually send it to the backend service. In order to export data in bulk, just put all objects into an&nbsp;<code>IEnumerable</code>&nbsp;container and pass it into&nbsp;<code>Create</code>&nbsp;as a parameter.</p> <h4>InvalidTimeZoneException exception</h4> <p>You may encounter an&nbsp;<code>InvalidTimeZoneException</code>&nbsp;exception that looks like:</p> <p>This means that one of the provided dates doesn&rsquo;t have a&nbsp;<code>DateTimeKind</code>. In order to fix this you update the date by calling&nbsp;<code>DateTime.SpecifyKind</code>.</p> <div> <div><code>DateTime date =&nbsp;</code><code>new</code>&nbsp;<code>DateTime(2013, 02, 19);</code></div> <div><code>date = DateTime.SpecifyKind(date, DateTimeKind.Utc);</code></div> </div> <h4>Getting the data back from the Backend</h4> <p>Now that we have some data, let&rsquo;s read the data back from the backend service.</p> <p>The first 2 steps of the process are the same as in the export process:</p> <ul> <li>Prepare backend service project link</li> <li>Create facade for working with required data store</li> </ul> <p>After you complete these steps, you can to call&nbsp;<code>GetAll</code>&nbsp;to get all object or&nbsp;<code>GetById</code>&nbsp;to get a specific object.</p> <p>Below is an example showing how to read back the record we created earlier. If you are following along, note that the ID for your player within the backend service will be different, so adjust the Guid value accordingly.</p> <div class="reCodeBlock" style="border: 1px solid #7f9db9; overflow-y: auto;"> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">private</code> <code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">void</code> <code style="color: #000000;">ReadData()</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span style="margin-left: 0px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">{</code></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 12px ! important;"><code style="color: #008200;">//Prepare backend service project link</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 12px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">var backend = </code><code style="color: #006699; font-weight: bold;">new</code> <code style="color: #000000;">EverliveApp(</code><code style="color: blue;">"ABC123apiKey"</code><code style="color: #000000;">);</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span><code>&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 3px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">var playerFacade = backend.WorkWith().Data&lt;Player&gt;();</code></span></span></div> <div style="background-color: #f8f8f8;"><span><code>&nbsp;</code><span style="margin-left: 3px ! important;"><code style="color: #000000;">}</code></span></div> </div> <h3>Final thoughts</h3>The best part of working with Telerik Backend Services is that there is no need to build any parsers or mapping logic. This is definitely much easier than using an XML-based data storage, SQL database or .Net object serialization, all of which require you to build both the read and the write logic, the handling for nulls and many other issues. With the Telerik Backend Services SDK, a correctly defined class is enough to transform the data from the backend service into a .Net object and vice versa.<br />
