Using Everlive Push Notifications Service in your native iOS app|Cloud|<p>Push notifications are useful for keeping users informed with timely and relevant contents. Push notifications can be sent regardless whether the app is running, inactive or in the background. Notifications can display an alert; play a distinctive sound or update badge on your app icon.</p> <p>In this post, I will walk through the process of enabling push notification for an app in Apple developer portal, upload the generated certificate to Everlive and finally register my device in Everlive to receive push notifications.</p> <p>Before you begin, note that you cannot test push notifications in iOS simulator. You need an iOS device as well as an Apple developer account. You also need to&nbsp;<a href="https://www.everlive.com/" target="_blank">sign up for Everlive</a>&nbsp;in order to send push notifications using its service.</p> <p>In this post I have created a provisioning profile from an App ID with push notification enabled. I then walked through the process of registering the device in Everlive and sent a notification using&nbsp;<em>curl</em>.&nbsp; Everlive and equivalent providers simplify the process of sending push notifications to your device. Apple Push Notification service transports and routes a notification from a given provider to a given device.</p> <p>It is possible to write your own provider, however in that case you have to manually configure the payload dictionary, validate device and deal with security.&nbsp; Moreover, each platform handles push notifications differently like Android uses Google cloud. In that case, you have to manually implement providers for each platform. Everlive on the other hand will take care of the platform specific details and relay your notifications to all associated devices without requiring you to go under the hood.</p> <p>Finally, I have skipped the configuration of Everlive SDK in Xcode, which is beyond the scope of this article. Please refer to the original SDK documentation @<a href="http://docs.everlive.com/" target="_blank"><em>http://docs.everlive.com</em>&nbsp;</a>to dig further.</p>
What is Cloud Code and Why Should You Care?|Cloud|<p>An easy-to-use Back-end-as-a-service (BaaS) can make rapidly developing your app not only a possibility, but an enjoyable experience. A good BaaS will work for simple "CRUD-based" (or "forms-over-data") apps as well as more complicated scenarios. The trouble is that when your app outgrows the simpler scenarios, you often need "hooks" on the server side for things like validation, record transformation and more. When you're using Everlive, this is where "Cloud Code" comes in.</p> <h2>What is Cloud Code?</h2> <p>"Cloud Code" enables you to execute JavaScript before or after "CRUD" (Create-Read-Update-Delete) operations in Everlive. So that means the following events have hooks to where you can execute "Cloud Code":</p> <ul> <li>Before Create</li> <li>After Create</li> <li>Before Read</li> <li>After Read</li> <li>Before Update</li> <li>After Update</li> <li>Before Delete</li> <li>After Delete</li> </ul> <p>(Sensing a pattern here? :-))</p> <p>As you'd expect, any of the&nbsp;<em>Before</em>&nbsp;events are executed&nbsp;<strong>before</strong>&nbsp;the request is processed. Conversely, any&nbsp;<em>After</em>&nbsp;events are executed<strong>after</strong>&nbsp;the request has been processed.</p> <p>These CRUD hooks are available on any Content Type you create (as well as the built-in Users Content Type).</p> <h2>How do You Use It?</h2> <p>While you can upload JavaScript files to Everlive, most of the time (at least initially), you will be using Everlive's web interface to add cloud code. To use the web interface, simply follow these steps:</p> <ul> <li>Log into Everlive</li> <li>Pick the Project</li> <li>Click on the "Types" link (on the left)</li> <li>Select the Content Type for which you want to create Cloud Code</li> <li>Click the "Cloud Code" link near the top right</li> </ul> <p>&nbsp;</p>
First Everlive-powered game released|Cloud|<p>We contacted them to get more information on how they used Everlive in their game and what was the development experience with our service. It turned out to be a really interesting story, so we decided to share it with everyone here, on our official blog.</p> <p>In the following paragraphs you will learn how the developers from Enless Soft used Everlive to make a great cloud-enabled app with minimum efforts. The following Everlive features and concepts will be covered or mentioned:</p> <ul> <li>Security system</li> <li>.NET SDK</li> <li>File storage</li> <li>Data storage</li> <li>Client data synchronization</li> <li>Master key access</li> <li>Cloud code</li> <li>Power fields</li> </ul> <p>About the game</p> <p>As mentioned above, Jigsaw Puzzles HD is a picture puzzle game. Everything there is about images. The game turns them into jigsaw puzzles and challenges you to match all the pieces. You can read more and download the game from its&nbsp;<a href="http://bit.ly/1aDD3JO" target="_blank">official page in the Windows Store</a>.</p> <p>We&rsquo;ve tried to present the whole story here: from the problems through their actual solution and implementation in Everlive to the plans for the future.</p> <p>How it all started</p> <p>Jigsaw Puzzles HD is a successor of&nbsp;<a href="http://bit.ly/wt7g5w" target="_blank">Jigsolve Me!</a>, a picture puzzle game for Windows Phone. Jigsolve Me! was one of the first apps that Enless Soft released for Windows Phone, around two years ago.<a href="http://blogs.telerik.com/images/default-source/everlive-blog-posts/jigsolve-me!-screenshot-gallery-png.png?sfvrsn=2"></a></p> <p>The devs really wanted to have a Windows 8 version of the game. They planned to add some new features and additional means to monetize their app. The Windows Phone version only had &ldquo;free&rdquo; and &ldquo;paid&rdquo; versions, and the new version had to have in-app purchases.</p> <p>Challenges</p> <p>Of course, while the devs were planning the porting of the game to the new platform, they faced some challenges and had to make decisions on how to overcome them.</p> <p><strong>Size of images</strong></p> <p>The Windows 8 version of the game is targeted on tablets and desktop PCs. This means the images have to be in much higher resolution, making them large in size. To enable this the images must be downloaded on demand, not included in the installation package.</p> <p><strong>Dynamically adding new images</strong></p> <p>The developers wanted to be able to constantly add new images to the game. They wanted to enable in-app purchases as a means to monetize their app and wanted to be able to release many paid image packs without releasing new version of the app to the marketplace.</p> <p><strong>Integrating the Windows Phone version</strong></p> <p>The Windows Phone version of the app must also be updated to support the new features and new ways to monetize. For this all the data must be and infrastructure must be shared so that users have seamless experience.</p> <p><strong>Pricing</strong></p> <p>Last but not least comes the pricing. Enless Soft is a startup company and it is important for them to have a service that can scale along with them. It was very important for them to have a low starting price and only pay real money when they make real money.</p>

Getting Started with Telerik Everlive - Your Cloud-Based Backend Service|Cloud|<p>Imagine yourself developing a new web or hybrid mobile application. One of your first major considerations is probably going to be your application's backend data. Are you leveraging an existing database server? Are you writing your own services layer on top of that database? Or do you have to start even further back and provision hardware or a VM, setup a database, create tables and views, and write stored procedures? The complexity of the backend can be overwhelming to many developers, especially those who have been solely focused on frontend development for some time now. Well today I'd like to walk you through a relatively new offering from Telerik - and that is Telerik Everlive. Telerik Everlive is your&nbsp;<a href="http://www.telerik.com/everlive" title="Telerik BaaS solution">"Backend as a Service" (BaaS)</a>&nbsp;which allows you to move your database into the cloud with an automatically generated RESTful service layer, file storage, user management, and notifications all bundled together. Fear the database no more, with Telerik Everlive we handle the heavy lifting for you - all you need to do is write your code!</p> <h2>Say "Cloud" One More Time...&nbsp;</h2> <p>I know. While "the cloud" is one of the more overused phrases in IT these days, it is useful to think of Telerik Everlive as helping organizations to move away from the hardware/software provisioning headaches of the past to a reliable service that requires very little oversight. And yes Telerik Everlive does live in "the cloud" - which really means that we have a lot of servers with a lot of redundancy to give you the uptime that your application's backend requires.</p> <p>This also means speed and scalability. Gone are the days when you have to add more hardware or tweak your own server settings to account for spikes in traffic. Telerik Everlive's infrastruture was built from the ground up to accommodate such heavy usage.</p> <h2>But What is Telerik Everlive, Really?</h2> <p>I have only emphasized one aspect of Telerik Everlive so far: data storage and management (essentially replacing your traditional database server). However, Telerik Everlive is really a set of other services, which can best be broken down into the following:</p> <ul> <li>Data and File Storage</li> <li>User Management</li> <li>Cloud Code</li> <li>Backend Portal</li> <li>Notifications</li> </ul> <p>While today we are going to focus on the "data" aspect of Telerik Everlive, it's important to acknowledge these other services to point out the value that they can bring to your application development.</p> <p><strong>User Management</strong>&nbsp;- Telerik Everlive allows you to easily add user authentication, user authorization, and user management to your app - starting with using popular&nbsp;<a href="http://oauth.net/">oAuth</a>&nbsp;providers such as Google, Facebook, and Microsoft.</p> <p><strong>Cloud Code</strong>&nbsp;- With Telerik Everlive's Cloud Code, you have the ability to add custom business logic and validators in JavaScript that run on the server. You don't have to replicate server-side code on the client and you don't have to worry about exposing business logic to prying client eyes either.</p> <p><strong>Backend Portal</strong>&nbsp;- Telerik Everlive comes with a complete web-based interface for managing all aspects of your app data. You can create new objects (think of them as database tables or views) and manage your users all from one consistent interface.</p> <p><strong>Notifications</strong>&nbsp;- Telerik Everlive makes it easy to deliver email notifications to your users using Cloud Code. You can also send push notifications if you are developing a native or hybrid mobile app on the iOS, Android, or Windows Phone platforms.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p>
